  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d530e514-158d-43d3-a809-2792eff3ebb1'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14673490228109841039">Maia D’Apliese and her five sisters gather together at their childhood home, “Atlantis”—a fabulous, secluded castle situated on the shores of Lake Geneva—having been told that their beloved father, who adopted them all as babies, has died. Each of them is handed a tantalizing clue to her true heritage—a clue which takes Maia across the world to a crumbling mansion in Rio d</span>
  <span id="freeText14673490228109841039" style="display:none">Maia D’Apliese and her five sisters gather together at their childhood home, “Atlantis”—a fabulous, secluded castle situated on the shores of Lake Geneva—having been told that their beloved father, who adopted them all as babies, has died. Each of them is handed a tantalizing clue to her true heritage—a clue which takes Maia across the world to a crumbling mansion in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil. Once there, she begins to put together the pieces of her story and its beginnings.<br /><br />Eighty years earlier in Rio’s Belle Epoque of the 1920s, Izabela Bonifacio’s father has aspirations for his daughter to marry into the aristocracy. Meanwhile, architect Heitor da Silva Costa is devising plans for an enormous statue, to be called Christ the Redeemer, and will soon travel to Paris to find the right sculptor to complete his vision. Izabela—passionate and longing to see the world—convinces her father to allow her to accompany him and his family to Europe before she is married. There, at Paul Landowski’s studio and in the heady, vibrant cafes of Montparnasse, she meets ambitious young sculptor Laurent Brouilly, and knows at once that her life will never be the same again.<br /><br />In this sweeping, epic tale of love and loss—the first in a unique, spellbinding series of seven novels—Lucinda Riley showcases her storytelling talent like never before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14673490228109841039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/45735127-jane-brown"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/45735127-jane-brown">Jane Brown</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    All the way through this book I kept thinking about the little boy and what he said to Bel. Then on the last page of the book there is reference to 'M<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    All the way through this book I kept thinking about the little boy and what he said to Bel. Then on the last page of the book there is reference to 'Morning Mood' again. But there were only 15 years maximum between the age of Bel and the boy so he can't have been Pa Salt! What is the connection then? And how did Pa Salt make his fortune? I was left thinking that Pa Salt might not be dead. And if he isn't why would he go to the extremes of faking his own death? I have never been so engrossed in the characters of any book before. So many unanswered questions, I only finished it this afternoon and I can't stop thinking about it. My imagination is running away with me! Well done to Lucinda, she certainly had me hooked. Can't wait for the sequel. Jane <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/40409733-sarah">Sarah</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Having read the first three books I can say that they work as stand-alones as they all give the necessary bit of introduction that you need at the beg<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Having read the first three books I can say that they work as stand-alones as they all give the necessary bit of introduction that you need at the beginning. That being said, I would still recommend starting at the beginning if you think you're going to want to read the whole series - and there are some threads that weave through all books.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=cultural-brazil">cultural-brazil</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260774697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7992465250587416707">When I began reading <b>The Seven Sisters</b> I had no idea it was to be part of a series.....which is good....and bad.<p>This first book is <i>not</i> the story of seven sisters, but just <b>one</b> of six adopted female babies who grow up as privileged children <i>(named for constellations)</i> at an amazing island home in Switzerland called Atlantis......and when Pa Salt dies, each of the six grown women are given a private letter with a secret clue to their past.</p><p>Maia, an astoundingly beautiful interpreter, who translates </p></span>
  <span id="freeText7992465250587416707" style="display:none">When I began reading <b>The Seven Sisters</b> I had no idea it was to be part of a series.....which is good....and bad.<p>This first book is <i>not</i> the story of seven sisters, but just <b>one</b> of six adopted female babies who grow up as privileged children <i>(named for constellations)</i> at an amazing island home in Switzerland called Atlantis......and when Pa Salt dies, each of the six grown women are given a private letter with a secret clue to their past.</p><p>Maia, an astoundingly beautiful interpreter, who translates books for authors is the oldest sister and the first to return to her roots to investigate her beginnings.....and what an excellent story she has.....I truly did not want to put it down.....and the ending......What?!?!?!?.....surprise! surprise!</p><p>Anyway, all I can say is that this wonderful work of fictional romance has so much substance and interesting bits of past history that you won't want to stop reading, and although parts of the romantic interlude(s) were somewhat predictable, I was never bored.....but the worst part of it all.....seriously.....is waiting for Book 2! I want to read it now!!!</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="7992465250587416707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1281454692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281454692" />
    <a title="Sandy Lenahan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26236011-sandy-lenahan"><img alt="Sandy Lenahan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454289362p2/26236011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1281454692?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy Lenahan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy Lenahan" href="/user/show/26236011-sandy-lenahan">Sandy Lenahan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26236011-sandy-lenahan?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26236011-sandy-lenahan?shelf=books-i-just-couldn-t-finish">books-i-just-couldn-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26236011-sandy-lenahan?shelf=reads-of-2015">reads-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1281454692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2178878136550296578">I guess I'm in the minority on this one because I hated it. I'd pick it up to read then put it down again over and over till finally I tossed it on the bedside table with a disgusted "fugeddaboudit" that would've made my mother-in-law proud (she's from New Yawk). The characters are about as believable as the tooth fairy. The mysterious father who adopted the 6 shallow and very annoying girls right down to the trusted live-in housekeeper with a heart of gold were right out of a bad soap opera. I </span>
  <span id="freeText2178878136550296578" style="display:none">I guess I'm in the minority on this one because I hated it. I'd pick it up to read then put it down again over and over till finally I tossed it on the bedside table with a disgusted "fugeddaboudit" that would've made my mother-in-law proud (she's from New Yawk). The characters are about as believable as the tooth fairy. The mysterious father who adopted the 6 shallow and very annoying girls right down to the trusted live-in housekeeper with a heart of gold were right out of a bad soap opera. I guess since Brangelina made adopting from 3rd world countries chic that's what single white billionaires who live on an island in Switzerland do these days. Not that any of his adult daughters know anything about the man, which they say many times as they try to process his sudden and mysterious death &amp; burial at sea - come on, this has Days of Our Lives written all over it.<br /><br />Bottom line-there's just so many good books out there to read that you don't want to waste your time on this one, it's a stinker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2178878136550296578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="xhr_comment_photo">

  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a style="font-weight:bold" href="/user/show/54821336-sarah-beck-derna">Sarah Beck-Derna</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer1740397096843933395">Flat writing and unbelievable characters. Inconsistencies such as the protagonist deciding to text her sisters to call her and her sister calling back</span>
  <span id="freeText1740397096843933395" style="display:none">Flat writing and unbelievable characters. Inconsistencies such as the protagonist deciding to text her sisters to call her and her sister calling back to say she could tell something had happened by the tone of her voice. This irritated me. None of the girls have any idea what their father did for a living despite Wikipedia being mentioned later on in the novel. The protagonist narrates in the first person, she is meant to be a writer herself (A bad one it would seem). But as the novel progressed to historical times, I started to forgive the quality of writing. It is a good concept. I enjoyed it as I would a meal of junk food. But I don’t think I could repeat in the near future.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8748591079868591869">This book was recommended by a friend, but I couldn't push through reading more than 100 pages. It started out well, but I had to stop after reading one implausible scene after another. I shouldn't have read past the part of the book where "Pa Salt" adopts a baby girl and brings her to his island called (what else) Atlantis, leaving her in the care of her guardian before flying off to parts unknown, repeating that five more times for a total of six adopted baby girls.   <span id="freeText8748591079868591869" style="display:none">This book was recommended by a friend, but I couldn't push through reading more than 100 pages. It started out well, but I had to stop after reading one implausible scene after another. I shouldn't have read past the part of the book where "Pa Salt" adopts a baby girl and brings her to his island called (what else) Atlantis, leaving her in the care of her guardian before flying off to parts unknown, repeating that five more times for a total of six adopted baby girls. Really? Pa Salt dies suddenly and is buried at sea before any of his adult daughters are informed of his death. Seriously??? I'll spare you the details of the other ridiculous plot lines. Maybe there's something wrong with me...this is a highly-rated book, but I felt as if I was reading a Harlequin romance novel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9745237247383091407"> <i>“Remember, even if we can’t see them, those we love are always with us” </i><br/> ----Lucinda Riley<br/><br/>Lucinda Riley, an Irish international best-selling author, have spun a terrific and absolutely stunning saga of six sisters in an all new series of <i>The Seven Sisters</i>. <i>The Seven Sisters</i> is the first book and the story of first/eldest sister, Maia.   <span id="freeText9745237247383091407" style="display:none"> <i>“Remember, even if we can’t see them, those we love are always with us” </i><br /> ----Lucinda Riley<br /><br />Lucinda Riley, an Irish international best-selling author, have spun a terrific and absolutely stunning saga of six sisters in an all new series of <i>The Seven Sisters</i>. <i>The Seven Sisters</i> is the first book and the story of first/eldest sister, Maia. This is her journey to search for her roots after her adoptive father's death.<br /><br /><b>Synopsis: </b><br /><i>Maia D'Apliése and her five sisters gather together at their childhood home, 'Atlantis' - a fabulous, secluded castle situated on the shores of Lake Geneva - having been told that their beloved father, the elusive billionaire they call Pa Salt, has died. Maia and her sisters were all adopted by him as babies and, discovering he has already been buried at sea, each of them is handed a tantalising clue to their true heritage - a clue which takes Maia across the world to a crumbling mansion in Rio de Janeiro in Brazil. Once there, she begins to put together the pieces of where her story began . . .<br /><br />Eighty years earlier, in the Belle Epoque of Rio, 1927, Izabela Bonifacio's father has aspirations for his daughter to marry into aristocracy. Meanwhile, architect Heitor da Silva Costa is working on a statue, to be called Christ the Redeemer, and will soon travel to Paris to find the right sculptor to complete his vision. Izabela - passionate and longing to see the world - convinces her father to allow her to accompany him and his family to Europe before she is married. There, at Paul Landowski's studio and in the heady, vibrant cafés of Montparnasse, she meets ambitious young sculptor Laurent Brouilly, and knows at once that her life will never be the same again. </i><br /><br />Although the story is a fictional account of a woman who's roots leads her to the high road of Rio de Janeiro where the story again takes us eighty years back in time when the French sculptor Paul Landowski and the Brazilian engineer Heitor da Silva Costa were working on Christ the Redeemer's statue. Some characters in the book are drawn straight from the pages of our world history, but the stories going in and around their lives were all fictional! <br /><br />Maia D'Apliése is the eldest of the six sisters and they all have been adopted by a wealthy billionaire, whom they used to call as 'Pa Salt'. They grew up in their adoptive father's palatial home by the shores of Lake Geneva. But Pa Salt is dead now and acting upon his dying wish to trade back to their own roots, Maia embarks on a Brazilian journey, where she not only discovers love, but also learns about one of the greatest legend of Brazil. Read this book to find out the rest of the story!<br /><br />In one words, I'd describe this book as a truly enchanting masterpiece that to only takes us back in time but also takes us those exotic lands - the experience of which we can almost feel on our skin. Sadly, at the end of the book, I forgot this was a fictional story, and I'm still in belief with the story of Izabel and Christ the Redeemer's statue, since the author made her story so very convincing enough to fall for the trap.<br /><br />The writing is completely fabulous that will spell-bind you with it's fairytale essence. Yes, this story is nothing short of a fairytale- a castle, a damsel in distress, flies away to find her roots, falls in love, finds a beautiful back-story that is connected with the history of Brazil. The author have unfolded the stories of Maia and Izabel strikingly and consecutively, with Izabel's story breaking at such vital points that will burn you out with anticipation. The prose is eloquent and evocative enough to keep you turning the pages of the book till it's very end. Moreover, the articulate conversation between the characters keeps you glued to it. The emotional pull in this book is quite strong, and since the story unfolds from Maia's POV, who happens to be an deeply emotional human being. And reading about which will simply make you feel as if the author have poured all her emotions into her words.<br /><br />This story has many layers and each intricately layered is written with enough compassion and depth. Moreover, there is also enough space that the author have left with her story for us to judge us from our perspective. The characters are well-crafted and exceptionally brilliant. From the first chapter of the book, the author gives us a character sketch of all the six sisters along with their nurse and their father to understand about their behavior briefly. And in Izabel's story, we can feel each and every character, like from the moment Izabel described her would-be husband, Gustavo in her words, I could almost imagine how he would behave in front of Izabel. <br /><br />While reading the book, I could feel the tropical heat of Brazil and that faint smell of the sea on my tongue. Not only Brazil, there's also Paris- and Paris happens to be the place where Izabel first fell in love and so you can imagine, the author turned the narrow lanes and elegant cafes of Paris into a romantic one and the Paris part completely transfixed my mind and soul with it's flawless beauty. <br /><br /><b>Verdict: </b> <i>So what are you waiting for? Take a trip down to the tropical paradise- Brazil and the romantic city- Paris with Lucinda Riley's new book that unfolds the journey of a woman searching for her roots. </i><br /><br /><b>Courtesy: </b> <i>Thanks to the author's publicist, for giving me an opportunity to read and review her book. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9745237247383091407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=women-s-fiction-of-no-substance">women-s-fiction-of-no-substance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=sagas">sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=love-finds-a-way">love-finds-a-way</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1504122287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6431863294417424068">The Seven Sisters by Lucinda Riley is the first book in a new series. The rich "Pa Salt" who has six adopted adult daughters, mysteriously added to his single parent family under circumstances unique and never explained to each one, has died. Just as mysteriously, his body has been whisked away and dropped into the ocean in a lead-lined coffin, leaving the grief stricken women who gather at their opulent Swiss lakeside home with no real closure. They are left, however, with trust funds, the loca</span>
  <span id="freeText6431863294417424068" style="display:none">The Seven Sisters by Lucinda Riley is the first book in a new series. The rich "Pa Salt" who has six adopted adult daughters, mysteriously added to his single parent family under circumstances unique and never explained to each one, has died. Just as mysteriously, his body has been whisked away and dropped into the ocean in a lead-lined coffin, leaving the grief stricken women who gather at their opulent Swiss lakeside home with no real closure. They are left, however, with trust funds, the locations of their births, a letter to each from their father and a clue to their identity if they wish to follow up (which of course they will, because that's the centre most theme of this series.).<br /><br />The sisters are named for the stars of the Pleides Constellation, used by sailors to find their way. Maia, the eldest begins her search by travelling to Rio di Janero, Brazil. <br /><br />This novel, and I will assume those to come, will fit into the genre of "women's romantic fiction", and will be enjoyed by these aficionados. Riley does a terrific job of switching eras between the related subplots, and fictionalizing the history of the creation of "Cristos", the huge statue outside Rio, to make it part of the texture of her worldly and very romantic tale. Present day Maia, as with many of this type of genre's protagonists, and her sisters are irritatingly reticent in their decision making (starting with looking for their ancestry). Maia is unbecomingly hesitant, and less than resourceful until a handsome historian does the work for her in actively researching leads. Her 1920’s counterpart Bel actually has more spunk than she does. <br /><br />Ah, well. Pieces of the mystery remain unsolved as the novel moves to Ally, the next sister. Riley has great technique and a formula that works for her and obviously, with its 4.16 rating, her faithful following. I think that I'm becoming a bit underwhelmed with this genre, a fault of sheer familiarity through exposure to earlier authors' equally good efforts and which I in my younger years I read in great quantity. My young self would enthusiastically rate this 4.00 at least but my more jaded less impressed self says, I liked it, but I'm not going to follow the series... It was okay. Which means a rating of 3.00 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6431863294417424068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5372502843794235317" style="display:none">Well...well...well....what an enjoyable ride this was. Lucinda Riley managed to keep me fully engrossed in this tale of the oldest sister, Maia. I loved how the clues were managed and, most importantly, that this series will only rely on telling each sister's story separately. Therefore, you really get to know where each one came from, their past and present story. This one focused on Maia and great-grandmother, Bel. How I loved Bel and her destiny. Her story was a pleasure and, also, painful to hear but I loved it nonetheless. Awe...Laurent:) I also loved Lake Geneva, Atlantis, Rio, and Paris. Reading is the only way I can travel these days, &amp; I'm so happy that I got to go to some exotic places! Very well written, great story, loved the characters, the places....well, just about everything! I definitely can't wait to hear the rest of the sisters stories! <div id="review_1199372383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199372383" />
    <a title="Claire Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14026987-claire-robinson"><img alt="Claire Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431471072p2/14026987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1199372383?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire Robinson" href="/user/show/14026987-claire-robinson">Claire Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23256764-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14026987-claire-robinson?shelf=shit-hot-series">shit-hot-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1199372383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9734259664281838982">4.5 - <b>Now was the time to discover who I was. Where I came from. And where I belonged.</b> Stars!<br/><br/><i>The Seven Sisters</i> is a book that you will struggle to put down once you start reading. The co-ordinates on an Armillary Sphere set off a chain of events, which send Maia D’aplise on an adventure of a life time.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430832338i/14767036._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Set in the present (2007) the story is begins on Lake Geneva, in Switzerland where Maia and her sisters; Ally, Star, Cece, Tiggy and Electra all meet up at the family home for the reading off their</span>
  <span id="freeText9734259664281838982" style="display:none">4.5 - <b>Now was the time to discover who I was. Where I came from. And where I belonged.</b> Stars!<br><br><i>The Seven Sisters</i> is a book that you will struggle to put down once you start reading. The co-ordinates on an Armillary Sphere set off a chain of events, which send Maia D’aplise on an adventure of a life time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430832338i/14767036._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Set in the present (2007) the story is begins on Lake Geneva, in Switzerland where Maia and her sisters; Ally, Star, Cece, Tiggy and Electra all meet up at the family home for the reading off their adoptive fathers will, this reading and the information provided sends Maia off to Rio to investigate further. In the course of her searching we go back to the late 1920’s, and are given the story of Maia’s Great Grandmother, Izabela Bonifacio and her travels to Paris as well as her life in Rio, her loves and her losses along the way. <br><br><b>”Hiding away from the world never works, because you still have to meet yourself in the mirror every morning.”</b><br><br>I loved this book; it is a beautifully written, visual and imaginatively stimulating read. The author manages to describe and give nuance to everywhere the women go, the people they meet and the stories they are telling. I also liked that as the story progressed the slight parallels between Maia’s current life and Bel’s previous life although not apparent initially become more clear as each facet of Izobela’s life with her husband Gustavo, and then her lover Laurent develops.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430832338i/14767037._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Set against the backdrop of the planning, and building of the great <i>Christ the Redeemer</i> statue, the Wall Street crash and everything that happened in-between, Bel’s story was what actually shone through this book for me, even though it is the secondary part of the book to Maia’s story, I just fell in love with her and the struggles she faced with the pressures of her life, her familial expectations and ultimately the decision she has to make, between her hearts happiness, and her families future.<br><br><b>I sit here looking up at the stars and wish with all my heart we had met at a different moment in time.</b><br><br>I have a feeling that this series will be one of the few that I will make time to go back and revisit many times over the years, and I cannot wait for the next sister to go on her own voyage of discovery.<br><br>ARC generously provided via Netgalley, in exchange for the above honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9734259664281838982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1199372383">

<span id="freeTextContainer17249190702758801839">Overally,this was a good read and definately a page turner,only i felt the book could be 200 pages shorter.There were pages that nothing happened as the story dwelled on the same things over and over again.I think that Belle's story could have covered less pages,all this uneccessary chatter did not add something essential to the main story.However,i enjoyed it despite all the cliches like the pretty rich girl who suffocates in her wealthy environment,the ugly husband and the gorgeous french love</span>
  <span id="freeText17249190702758801839" style="display:none">Overally,this was a good read and definately a page turner,only i felt the book could be 200 pages shorter.There were pages that nothing happened as the story dwelled on the same things over and over again.I think that Belle's story could have covered less pages,all this uneccessary chatter did not add something essential to the main story.However,i enjoyed it despite all the cliches like the pretty rich girl who suffocates in her wealthy environment,the ugly husband and the gorgeous french lover,the strict and sour mother-in-law etc.We've read about this a hundred of times and we've also seen such plots in mexican and brazilian soap operas.You'll probably wonder why i'm giving it four stars,well,for starters it was beautifully written and all these descriptions of Rio were so vivid that made me see,feel and fall in love with Brazil plus the background story of the creation of Christo's monument fascinated me.Definately,that book made me want to visit Brazil.Up to the 2nd book now!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_1167787346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167787346" />
    <a title="Carmen Blankenship " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5586759-carmen-blankenship"><img alt="Carmen Blankenship " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402524243p2/5586759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167787346?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen Blankenship " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen Blankenship " href="/user/show/5586759-carmen-blankenship">Carmen Blankenship </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586759-carmen-blankenship?shelf=netgally-reading-list">netgally-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586759-carmen-blankenship?shelf=adored">adored</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167787346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14527363941419077209">I hate only being able to give this book a 5 star rating. It would rate it 10 moons if I could. Lucinda Riley's writing is beautiful. I simply don't know what other adjective to use. Pick one. Seamless, whimsical, witty, smart, lyrical, enthralling, enchanting.... see? I simply cannot pick one. <br/><br/>The Seven Sisters is the first installment in an exciting new series based 6 Sisters all adopted by their beloved Pa Salt. They grew up in Switzerland on their very own island. Their mysterious father has</span>
  <span id="freeText14527363941419077209" style="display:none">I hate only being able to give this book a 5 star rating. It would rate it 10 moons if I could. Lucinda Riley's writing is beautiful. I simply don't know what other adjective to use. Pick one. Seamless, whimsical, witty, smart, lyrical, enthralling, enchanting.... see? I simply cannot pick one. <br /><br />The Seven Sisters is the first installment in an exciting new series based 6 Sisters all adopted by their beloved Pa Salt. They grew up in Switzerland on their very own island. Their mysterious father has always been fabulously wealthy and eccentric. There is no luxury these girls did not grow up with, except the knowledge of exactly what their father did and at times his presence. Regardless of this they all loved him dearly and treasure their own memories. When the get word that Pa Salt has died they all come home. <br /><br />This installment is about the eldest sister Maia D’Apliese. Upon the reading of their fathers estate the sisters are all handed a clue as their true origins. From here the journey begins. <br /><br />The Seven Sisters is a long book but you do not realize it. You simply go where Lucinda Riley decides to take you and real world be damned. The only thing keeping from being mortified that it is over is the knowledge that there are more books to come. <br /><br />I cannot wait to unravel the mystery as to who Pa Salt really was, the true stories about the adoptions and origins of the other sisters. <br /><br />This book is exquisite and will definitely be re-read in the future.<br />Thank you Netgalley and Atria Books for the chance to read this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2906521819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906521819" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20793916-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492744200p2/20793916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906521819?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/20793916-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20793916-melissa?shelf=nook-books">nook-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20793916-melissa?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906521819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9164838537576907348">I tried so hard to find something to like about this book as it came highly recommended by a friend (I'm sorry Laura, I really tried!), but in the end I found it way too problematic: <br/><br/><b>Too much suspension of disbelief</b> - I cannot imagine a situation in which a single man could adopt six babies (all girls, no less) and bring them to live at his very private and secluded home without raising a field of red flags with any and all agencies involved. And then all of these six girls grow to adulthood wit</span>
  <span id="freeText9164838537576907348" style="display:none">I tried so hard to find something to like about this book as it came highly recommended by a friend (I'm sorry Laura, I really tried!), but in the end I found it way too problematic: <br /><br /><b>Too much suspension of disbelief</b> - I cannot imagine a situation in which a single man could adopt six babies (all girls, no less) and bring them to live at his very private and secluded home without raising a field of red flags with any and all agencies involved. And then all of these six girls grow to adulthood without ever once questioning what their father does to make all his money? How do they all know nothing about him? Its a ridiculous premise from the start. <br /><br /><b>Awful dialogue</b> - Pleases and thank yous are used like punctuation. Names are overused to an absurd degree as if the author thinks her readers will forget who is talking from one sentence to the next. Everything is stiff and unnatural and, depending on the content, sometimes painfully awkward. I dare anyone to read this book aloud...it's like the author has never held a conversation with another human being.<br /><br /><b>Horribly condescending love interests</b> - And not just the ones populating the historical segment of this story where it makes at least some sense. I found Floriano (a character set in 2007) extremely problematic. He constantly tells Maia how she should or should not feel and criticizes her life choices and emotional responses despite barely knowing her. At one point the author finds it necessary to have Floriano remind Maia that she has just lost her father and that this will have an effect on her emotions. Tell me Lucinda Riley...if your father just died, would you need someone to remind you?<br /><br /><b>Superficiality</b> - In this book, beauty or lack of it is enough to damn or redeem any character. Izabela's fiance, Gustavo, is nothing but kind to her, but because he "looks like a ferret" he clearly is the worst possible thing in the universe. Instead, Izabela gravitates toward Laurent, who is very very very handsome, but beyond that has no further depth as a character. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Despite everything, Izabela chooses to return home to marry Gustavo and at this point Lucinda Riley seems to realize that she's made Gustavo much too likeable. He's ugly, so obviously he can't be likeable. So what does she do? She turns him into an unfeeling monster in the bedroom and Izabela also suddenly remembers that he always drank a lot at parties. Voila! Gustavo must be an alcoholic. This kind of retrofitting felt so sloppy and forced that my knee-jerk reaction was to sympathize with Gustavo the rest of the story and despise Izabela and Laurent. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I could keep going, but I won't. Suffice it to say that I disliked this book strongly and do not recommend to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9164838537576907348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1109301899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109301899" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546484-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500388520p2/546484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109301899?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/546484-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781447274933" href="/book/show/23274807-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109301899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer610174009780570198">The seven sisters of the title are the D'Apliese sisters; there are actually only six of them, so that's the first mystery of this story. These women were all adopted as babies and brought up by the incredibly wealthy Pa Salt, on a beautiful estate in Geneva, Switzerland. Pa Salt has always been something of a mystery, a wealthy single man bringing up six beautiful adopted daughters, with no partner, just his trusted housekeeping staff to assist him. None of the girls really know how Pa Salt mad</span>
  <span id="freeText610174009780570198" style="display:none">The seven sisters of the title are the D'Apliese sisters; there are actually only six of them, so that's the first mystery of this story. These women were all adopted as babies and brought up by the incredibly wealthy Pa Salt, on a beautiful estate in Geneva, Switzerland. Pa Salt has always been something of a mystery, a wealthy single man bringing up six beautiful adopted daughters, with no partner, just his trusted housekeeping staff to assist him. None of the girls really know how Pa Salt made his fortune, but each of them have had a happy and full life, they are loved and they love each other.<br /><br />The sisters are summoned home when Pa Salt suddenly and unexpectedly dies. Just like his life, Pa's death and the arrangements after it have been precisely organised and each sister is left a letter and a clue to their true heritage. This first story is Maia, the eldest sister's story.<br /><br />Maia discovers that her roots are in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil and she travels there to the crumbling mansion that appears to be connected to her. It is in Rio that Maia's story really begins to come together and Lucinda Riley has cleverly weaved Maia's modern day story together with that of her great-grandmother Izabela Bonafacio. Also woven through this incredible novel is the story of how the statue of Christ the Redeemer was constructed, first in pieces in Paris, and then transported by boat to Rio where it was built piece by piece on top of the Corcovado mountain.<br /><br />The two cities; Paris and Rio are exquisitely drawn, the contrast between these two places is amazing, yet both of them are tantalising, and reading about them made me want to visit both of them. Izabel's time spent in the Montmarte area of Paris, populated by the bohemian artist community comes alive on the pages, with famous and familiar names taking centre stage. The contrast of Rio - the old, the new, the wealth, the poverty is exceptionally well done too.<br /><br />Maia and Izabela's stories are strikingly similar, with a theme of love and loss running through them both, and as Maia discovers more about her birth family history, she also realises more about herself, finally admitting to herself that some secrets can never be kept forever, and that she does not have to pay for one mistake for the rest of her life.<br /><br />The Seven Sisters is moving and absorbing, and I was absolutely transfixed by it. Please, don't be put off by the length of the book, it's over 600 pages, but I can assure you that these pages fly by and before you know it you will be at the end of the story and wishing so much that you had the next instalment ready to read next. Lucinda Riley is incredibly talented, her storytelling is precise and thrilling, she artfully combines the modern day story with events from history and has created something incredibly special. I'm desperate to read the next in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="610174009780570198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1296951748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296951748" />
    <a title="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm"><img alt="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555952303p2/5289134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296951748?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie • The Baking Bookworm" href="/user/show/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm">Laurie • The Baking Bookworm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289134-laurie-the-baking-bookworm?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296951748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5814800705173843480">My Review: This is a book about the power of family. I had read and adored one of Lucinda Riley's previous books, The Midnight Rose, last year so I was eager to read more from this acclaimed historical fiction author. I have to admit that it wasn't until I had finished reading The Seven Sisters that I realized that it is the first book in a seven book series - with each book focusing on a different sister's past. Cool premise but a big commitment from readers.<br/><br/>This first book focuses on Maia's se</span>
  <span id="freeText5814800705173843480" style="display:none">My Review: This is a book about the power of family. I had read and adored one of Lucinda Riley's previous books, The Midnight Rose, last year so I was eager to read more from this acclaimed historical fiction author. I have to admit that it wasn't until I had finished reading The Seven Sisters that I realized that it is the first book in a seven book series - with each book focusing on a different sister's past. Cool premise but a big commitment from readers.<br /><br />This first book focuses on Maia's search for her birth family and what she discovers is a gaggle of familial secrets on a different continent spanning generations. The secrets themselves weren't all that scandalous and were even predictable but this book held my interest for the most part. <br /><br />Honestly, I wanted to learn more about Maia and her adoptive family than her birth family. There were so many unanswered questions - I wanted to know more about Maia's adoptive father, Pa Salt, and his mysterious life as well as how and why he adopted six baby girls from all over the world. And yes I said six, not seven, because the seventh sister was never introduced. Mystery ... dun dun duuuuun. I suspect that Pa Salt has a lot more to his story than the reader (or the sisters) are privy to. His death was quite sudden and the way he died and even how he was buried was quite suspect. I sense that he had (and will have) a much larger role in each of his daughter's lives than they initially believed.<br /><br />The characters were interesting enough and quite diverse. I have to give credit to Riley for giving each of the sisters a very unique voice in the beginning of the book. Sadly we really don't get to see much more of the six sisters for the remainder of the book which was unfortunate because they were quite an interesting and diverse group of women. After Maia takes off to find her birth family the plot began to falter for me. As the story progressed it became less about Maia and more about Maia's great great grandmother, Izabella. While Izabella's story was fairly interesting it was Maia who I wanted to read about. And with the inclusion of Maia's grandmother and mother into the story, at times, it became hard to remember which generation we were talking about.<br /><br />The setting and history aspects are what enthralled me. Rio isn't a place that I've read about (let alone visited) before and while I know what the Christ the Redeemer (aka Christo) statue looks like it was interesting to learn more about its design and construction as well as a brief history of Brazil. The streets, people and culture of Rio was vividly described and I thoroughly enjoyed reading about this unique city as it's woven within a fictional tale.<br /><br />In the end, I can't say that I loved this book. It was good, not great. The pace dragged and it felt like it could have been condensed quite a bit and still kept the story in tact. The lackluster ending leaves readers with too many unanswered questions which may be used to entice readers to read the future books in the series but it left me feeling a little jilted if I'm being honest. Overall, this was a decent book but not up to par with some of Lucinda Riley's early works. <br /><br />My Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br /><br />**This book review can also be found on my blog, The Baking Bookworm (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thebakingbookworm.blogspot.ca">www.thebakingbookworm.blogspot.ca</a>) where I share hundreds of book reviews and my favourite recipes. **</span>
  <a data-text-id="5814800705173843480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1290272194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290272194" />
    <a title="The Lit Bitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4537892-the-lit-bitch"><img alt="The Lit Bitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547250681p2/4537892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290272194?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Lit Bitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Lit Bitch" href="/user/show/4537892-the-lit-bitch">The Lit Bitch</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23256764-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290272194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1041915106437893600">This novel took us to an exotic and beautiful location for a breathtaking story! One of the things that I loved the most was Riley took us to so many different beautiful locations and made us fall in love with each one: Geneva, Paris, London and Brazil….can I globe trot now please?!<br/><br/>The story itself was complex and beautifully constructed layers. Though it was long, I never felt like the story was ‘lengthy’ or ‘unnecessary’.<br/><br/>While it was long, the pages seemed to fly by! Riley has a wonderful way </span>
  <span id="freeText1041915106437893600" style="display:none">This novel took us to an exotic and beautiful location for a breathtaking story! One of the things that I loved the most was Riley took us to so many different beautiful locations and made us fall in love with each one: Geneva, Paris, London and Brazil….can I globe trot now please?!<br /><br />The story itself was complex and beautifully constructed layers. Though it was long, I never felt like the story was ‘lengthy’ or ‘unnecessary’.<br /><br />While it was long, the pages seemed to fly by! Riley has a wonderful way of capturing the readers interest and it’s almost like time stands still. While I was reading, I would look at my watch and be like ‘where has the time gone?!’.<br /><br />I was completely captivated from the very beginning. The clues that each person received were tantalizing and really caught my attention as a reader and made me want to know what they meant and how they fit.<br /><br />In that same vein, one thing that intrigued me about this series is that it is in fact a series. While there are all these different sisters with different clues, this book is about only one of the sisters. I am excited to read the other books that will come, the concept was well constructed and enticing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thelitbitch.com/2015/06/04/review-the-seven-sisters-a-novel-the-seven-sisters-1-by-lucinda-riley/" rel="nofollow noopener">See my full review here</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1041915106437893600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3100592276" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3100592276" />
    <a title="Shi ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75596954-shi"><img alt="Shi ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600693309p2/75596954.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3100592276?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shi ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shi ❀" href="/user/show/75596954-shi">Shi ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781529003451" href="/book/show/42181106-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75596954-shi?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75596954-shi?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75596954-shi?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75596954-shi?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3100592276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15653737563769744780">This was, overall, a lovely read. <br/><br/><i>The Seven Sisters</i> is a series that follows the lives and histories of - <b>surprise, surprise</b> -, seven sisters. The sisters have been adopted from all across the world by a man whom they call 'Pa Salt'. After his sudden death, the sisters gather in their childhood home: a castle in Geneva. There, they find out their adoptive father has given each of them clues to their roots. In the first instalment of the series, we follow Maia, the eldest sister, in her journey t</span>
  <span id="freeText15653737563769744780" style="display:none">This was, overall, a lovely read. <br /><br /><i>The Seven Sisters</i> is a series that follows the lives and histories of - <b>surprise, surprise</b> -, seven sisters. The sisters have been adopted from all across the world by a man whom they call 'Pa Salt'. After his sudden death, the sisters gather in their childhood home: a castle in Geneva. There, they find out their adoptive father has given each of them clues to their roots. In the first instalment of the series, we follow Maia, the eldest sister, in her journey to her birth country: Brazil. -<br /><br />The author utilises a frame narrative, where the main narrative sets the stage for a historical narrative, set in the late 1920s of Rio de Janeiro. There, we follow a young Italian-Brazilian woman, Izabela, whose father aims to ensure she marries into a wealthy family. But Izabela longs for independence and, engaged but yet unmarried, her father grants her permission to embark for the Old World together with the family of Heitor da Silva Costa, the architect who aims to construct what will eventually be known as the statue called Christ the Redeemer. During this journey, Izabela meets Laurent Brouilly, a young sculptor who introduces her to a life different from the strict, almost aristocratic lifestyle she has known in Brazil. <br /><br />Obviously, there are quite some cliches in this book, but it was quite well done. I liked the romance, and what I liked, even more, was the historical accuracy of the book and the manner in which it incorporates real historical figures. Riley did a lot of research, both into the history of Christ the Redeemer as well as the Seven Sisters themselves. The nickname for the sisters' father, 'Pa Salt' (who had a great love for the sea), strikes as odd, and I found out that it is an anagram for the God Atlas and the mother of the sisters, Pleione (Riley only used the 'P').<br /><br />The series is based on The Seven Sisters of the Pleiades (the sisters are named after these mythological sisters), and what immediately confused me was the fact that there are actually only really six sisters. Apparently, Riley has ideas for the seventh (missing) one, so that is definitely interesting. <br /><br />I only had a few points in the book I didn't like, namely the elusiveness and overall mystery that was Pa Salt. I know more answers will most likely materialise throughout the rest of the series (and I will definitely want to continue for now), but the idea of one man adopting six girls from all around the world and subsequently leaving them most of the time to be raised by a sort of nursemaid is just weird. Him dying and apparently knowing all about their origins and everything coming to the surface after his death seems like a great plot device, but too surreal to be true. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15653737563769744780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3104894414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3104894414" />
    <a title="~Sofia~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19899617-sofia"><img alt="~Sofia~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563875146p2/19899617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3104894414?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Sofia~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Sofia~" href="/user/show/19899617-sofia">~Sofia~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781529003451" href="/book/show/42181106-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3104894414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2850375617524690700">Lucinda Riley has been a firm favourite author of mine for a few years. I have read one book of hers so far, that being The Light Behind the Window, and it impressed me so much that I put her in my top authors list. However like those rare and amazing moments I wanted to savour her books and so have not read one since. Until now. <br/><br/>I recommended The Light Behind The Window to my nan who I knew would adore it like I did. She asked my opinion on The Seven Sisters series and I admitted I had not read</span>
  <span id="freeText2850375617524690700" style="display:none">Lucinda Riley has been a firm favourite author of mine for a few years. I have read one book of hers so far, that being The Light Behind the Window, and it impressed me so much that I put her in my top authors list. However like those rare and amazing moments I wanted to savour her books and so have not read one since. Until now. <br /><br />I recommended The Light Behind The Window to my nan who I knew would adore it like I did. She asked my opinion on The Seven Sisters series and I admitted I had not read it as I was ‘saving’ them. It doesn’t sound logical to me either but alas, once they are read I have to sit and await more to come so I would rather wait and savour them. Well that being said my nan does not have the same ideas as me and plowed ahead. She read the whole series (bar the ones left to be released, two to date) within a month and absolutely wholeheartedly fell in love with them. Which resulted in all 6 books winging there way to me for Christmas. My nan took my fate into her own hands and decided I needed to read these books immediately. And so on Christmas day I dipped my feet into Maia and her 5 sisters stories, and presently dived head first into this delightful story. <br /><br />The idea of creating a series about seven sisters had me hooked. Each book explores each of the sisters origins as they were adopted at birth. All books start on a sombre note with there adoptive father passing away. However as with all good books the end is sometimes just the beginning. <br /><br />Maia’s story takes us back to her great grandmother and her story is intimately linked to the history of Christ the Redeemer in Rio. Historical fiction is my favourite genre and I loved the historical element in this which goes back to the character of Izabela. It is a wondrous story that dips in and out of history and modern day. It includes a wide and generous amount from varied genres with romance being at the heart of it. Riley writes in a magnificent way transporting you to a myriad of locations. Each chapter draws you in and leaves you wanting more illicit drama. It really is fabulous and I literally cannot wait to dive straight back into the next book. <br /><br />The books in themselves are standalone stories however there are enough clues and little segments of wonder that lead through the whole series linking all books and creating its own novel through each of the sisters stories. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book to all and I am delighted and thankful to my nan for setting off year 2020 with a 5 star read! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2850375617524690700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5407684287772892369"><blockquote>Never let your fear decide your destiny. </blockquote><br/>A lot of people recommended this series to me, and I'm glad I finally got to it. I love the idea of seven adopted sisters from different places trying to track down their heritage using a quote and gps co-ordinates provided by their deceased adoptive father. This reminded me a little bit of the books I used to read when I was younger - easy historical fiction, with an element of romance.   <span id="freeText5407684287772892369" style="display:none"><blockquote>Never let your fear decide your destiny. </blockquote><br />A lot of people recommended this series to me, and I'm glad I finally got to it. I love the idea of seven adopted sisters from different places trying to track down their heritage using a quote and gps co-ordinates provided by their deceased adoptive father. This reminded me a little bit of the books I used to read when I was younger - easy historical fiction, with an element of romance. Although I don't normally read romance, I still enjoyed this book, which I read while lying on the beach. The historical fiction element was very interesting as I've never read anything about Rio de Janeiro set in the 1920's. The story behind the construction of Christ the Redeemer was very informative and well-researched. I will definitely be reading the rest of the series to see what happens to the other sisters. Perfect for holiday reading.<br /><br />The Story: The Seven Sisters tells the tale of six young women, all adopted by an enigmatic man for mysterious reasons. When he dies suddenly, he leaves behind a clue for each sister, and the past begins to unfold. This novel is the first in a new series about each sister’s path to uncover her history. The protagonist of this installment is the eldest sister, Maia. Her birth is tied to the sultry world of Rio de Janeiro, though it is the crushing reminder of love lost that drives her from her childhood home to confront the past.</span>

<div id="review_1340871784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1340871784" />
    <a title="Cameran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16033752-cameran"><img alt="Cameran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403098352p2/16033752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1340871784?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cameran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cameran" href="/user/show/16033752-cameran">Cameran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16033752-cameran?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340871784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5787185380188166095">After the sudden death of her adoptive father, Maia is provided clues should she decide to look into her past to discover where she came from. Thus, the story takes us to Brazil during the late 1920s at the time of the building of Christ the Redeemer and the life of the young woman who lives in the shadow of the mountain. Izabela is a beauty, and her father, to secure her a good match in order to raise the status of their immigrant family, uses her outer appearance to his advantage. A trip to Pa</span>
  <span id="freeText5787185380188166095" style="display:none">After the sudden death of her adoptive father, Maia is provided clues should she decide to look into her past to discover where she came from. Thus, the story takes us to Brazil during the late 1920s at the time of the building of Christ the Redeemer and the life of the young woman who lives in the shadow of the mountain. Izabela is a beauty, and her father, to secure her a good match in order to raise the status of their immigrant family, uses her outer appearance to his advantage. A trip to Paris before her wedding changes Izabela, however, as she meets a young sculptor and the two fall in love. As their story unfolds Maia comes to learn more about who she is and how she must change in the future in order to live her own life.<br /><br />Romance plays a large role in this story, but I unfortunately found the romances of the past and the present to be weak. Izabela and Laurent told me they were in love, rather than allow me to feel much of anything; Maia and Floriano had the most stilted conversations that I never saw what made him appeal to her at all. The love story of the past was also something that I had read numerous times before.<br /><br /><i>The Seven Sisters</i> serves as the first of what is to be a series about Maia and her five other sisters (yes, there is mysteriously only six of them), who were all adopted by a rich man they come to realize they knew nothing about. He has named each one of them after The Seven Sisters of the Pleiades, and the mystery surrounding him and why he adopted all of these girls is intriguing enough for me to lament how it was barely touched upon in Maia’s tale. If the next book in the series was to allow the next sister, who I presume will be Ally, to discover her past in a much more compact storyline (because this book did tend to drag) and focus more upon the mystery of Pa Salt then I will give it a shot. Otherwise, I can only recommend <i>The Seven Sisters</i> to those who truly love the author, want to visit Brazil in a story, or who are okay with romances that felt cookie-cutter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5787185380188166095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2529502878?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501108877" href="/book/show/23359097-the-seven-sisters">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2529502878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15867881793780945712">I wasn’t expecting to enjoy this as much as I did, the whole concept is unique and I’ve never read anything quite like it. The idea of the Seven Sisters and the mythology surrounding it is incredibly interesting! I only wish that we had learned more about the mythology, I’m really hoping other books in the series explore it in greater depth. I really enjoyed Maia as a character and I felt incredibly invested in her story and her journey to find her true heritage. It was an incredibly moving stor</span>
  <span id="freeText15867881793780945712" style="display:none">I wasn’t expecting to enjoy this as much as I did, the whole concept is unique and I’ve never read anything quite like it. The idea of the Seven Sisters and the mythology surrounding it is incredibly interesting! I only wish that we had learned more about the mythology, I’m really hoping other books in the series explore it in greater depth. I really enjoyed Maia as a character and I felt incredibly invested in her story and her journey to find her true heritage. It was an incredibly moving story and I love how it all played out in the end! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15867881793780945712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cUmwLhUbn07qP14Q63AlkmV6yYIAlichqUpXGL7BnF6aVxIIh3vLpyZpc5M6e5voN/Hy+8vVs8pV+qRUA3Cl2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rTd2MY5XmsiY5MGYdVGkEDdfUPCEhgIWvrAeNki7l0ZGKdQXHDfOIVSy7BukWhpqZdRriU/Flv1CAO169Qquwg==')})
  }

Van een proces is geen sprake: ze wordt monddood gemaakt. Haar geliefde Rembrandt van Rijn heeft daartoe opdracht gegeven.\nVanuit het spinhuis blikt Geertje Dircx terug op haar leven. Ze is van eenvoudige komaf, wordt jong weduwe maar weet zich te redden door als kindermeisje voor een welgestelde familie in Hoorn te werken. Als die betrekking eindigt, gaat ze naar Amsterdam en treedt ze in dienst bij Rembrandt van Rijn. Hij zoekt een kindermeisje voor zijn zoon Titus, omdat zijn vrouw Saskia ernstig ziek is. Na Saskia’s dood bestiert Geertje al snel het hele huishouden, zorgt voor Titus en voor de eenzame Rembrandt. Jarenlang leven ze als een getrouwd paar, en Rembrandt geeft haar de sieraden uit Saskia’s erfenis. Maar op een gegeven moment blijkt zijn liefde voor Geertje niets meer waard.   <span id="freeText7237246725612005245" style="display:none">AKA: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/460569.Lucinda_Edmonds" title="Lucinda Edmonds" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucinda Edmonds</a><br />Lucinda Riley was born in Ireland, and after an early career as an actress in film, theatre and television, wrote her first book aged twenty-four. Her books have been translated into thirty-seven languages and sold twenty-five million copies worldwide. She is a No.1 Sunday Times and New York Times bestseller.<br /><br />Lucinda is currently writing The Seven Sisters series, which tells the story of adopted sisters and is inspired by the mythology of the famous star cluster. It has become a global phenomenon, with each book in the series being a No.1 bestseller across the world. The series is currently in development with a major Hollywood production company.</span>
